The Kincheng Banking Corporation Suspended Operations Yesterday

Affected by the Inability of the Hong Kong Head Office to Sustain Operations

Whether Operations Will Resume Awaits a Reply from the Head Office

According to the Central News Agency, the Kincheng Banking Corporation at 300 Beijing Road, originally a branch of the Hong Kong Kincheng Savings Bank, suspended operations yesterday after receiving a telegram from its head office stating that it was unable to sustain operations and had ceased operations. The bank's permanent legal counsel, Lawyer Song Yunhui, issued a notice announcing the temporary suspension of operations, pending instructions from the head office, after which a decision would be made to liquidate or continue operations. According to a person in charge of Lawyer Song's firm, the branch has been established for approximately three years with a capital of 200,000 yuan. The manager is Tan Huiqing and the deputy manager and treasurer is Bai Hongji. Daily operations have been relatively stable. Currently, due to the closure of the head office, the branch has no way to operate independently, so suspension is inevitable. However, assets and liabilities are certain to offset each other. The lawyer's notice and the bank's history are detailed below:

Lawyer's Notice

Lawyer Song Yunhui's Agency Notice: According to the representative of the Shanghai Branch Co., Ltd. of Kincheng Banking Corporation, a telegram was suddenly received from the Hong Kong head office stating that the head office, being unable to maintain operations, has ceased operations. As to whether this branch should also cease operations, aside from seeking instructions from the head office, operations will be temporarily suspended today pending a reply. Please have your esteemed firm issue a notice on our behalf. Hence, this notice is issued on their behalf as above. January 5, 1935, Song Yunhui, Lawyer.

Bank History

The Kincheng Savings Bank Co., Ltd. was founded in Hong Kong in 1923 with a paid-up capital of one million Hong Kong dollars. In December 1924, it was registered with the Hong Kong government and also with the Ministry of Industry. The chairman is Feng Dachun, the supervisors are Huang Boyuan and Kuang Lesheng, and the general manager is Tan Xitian. It has two branches, one in Shanghai and one in Guangzhou. Recently, due to excessive investment in land mortgages, its cash flow was disrupted, forcing it to suspend operations. The Guangzhou branch has also suspended operations and is awaiting liquidation.

City Chamber of Commerce Explains Stamp Tax Still Applied as Before

Although New Law is Promulgated, It Has Not Been Implemented

Although the new Stamp Tax Law has been amended and enacted by the Legislative Yuan and promulgated by the National Government on December 8 last year, it has not yet been implemented. There has been much confusion in the city's business community, and many have inquired with the City Chamber of Commerce. According to a formal statement by Yan E'sheng, the secretary of the Chamber, although the new law has been promulgated, according to the final article of the law, the date of implementation will be determined by order. As the implementation date has not yet arrived, all bills and account books should still be stamped in accordance with the existing Stamp Tax Regulations. Once the National Government formally orders the implementation of the new law in the future, the Chamber will formally announce compliance. The Commercial Monthly Report of the Chamber previously compiled and printed a "Question and Answer Guide to Stamp Tax," which was sold at the office of the Monthly Report and was not distributed outside by staff. Since the formulation of the new Stamp Tax Law, the Chamber has not received the original text of the new law, so there have been no publications on the subject. Any publications being distributed outside are counterfeit and should be handed over to the police. Such counterfeit publications are bound to contain many errors, and if followed, will inevitably cause problems.

Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry Plans This Year's Fisheries Protection Plan

Divided into Three Categories: Regular Patrol, Roving, and Escort

Patrolling Vessels Responsible for Preventing Foreign Vessel Encroachment

The Fisheries Protection Office of the Ministry of Industry has drafted an outline of this year's fisheries protection plan and submitted it to the Ministry for review. A reporter from the New Voice News Agency has obtained the original text as follows:

Fishing Area Under Jurisdiction This office was reorganized from the Jiangzhe Area Marine Fisheries Administration, so the fishing area under its jurisdiction is temporarily limited to the two provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang. However, due to the small number of patrol vessels in this office, allocation is often difficult, and there is a tendency to focus on one area and neglect others. In May last year, a joint defense conference was held with the Coastal Patrol Office of the Ministry of Navy, the Third District of the Jiangsu Provincial Water Police Force, and the Second Brigade of the Zhejiang Water Police. It was decided that each area would be responsible for a section. The patrol locations assigned to this office are divided into three zones: (1) Waters such as Shenjiamen, Zhujia Island, Donghuoshan, Erxiongdi, Langgang, Haijiao, and Shenshan; (2) Waters such as Sheshan, Luohua (Lvhua), Huadao Mountain, Huanglong, Maji, Sijiao, and Beitingshan (Beidingxin); (3) Waters such as Zhoushan, Daishan, Changtu, Qushan, Qingbang, Miaozi Lake, and Daji Mountain.

Fishing Season The fishing season in Jiangsu and Zhejiang can be divided into spring, autumn, and winter seasons. According to the type of fish and the time and location of production, the main types can be divided into: (1) Large yellow croaker: Qushan, Daji Yang, Daishan, Huangda Yang, from the vernal equinox to the minor heat (most abundant from Grain Rain to the Start of Summer; also present in autumn); (2) Small yellow croaker: Lvsi Yang, Shenshan, Taohua, Huadao, Sheshan, Langgang, Lvhua, from the end of winter to the beginning of spring, from the vernal equinox to the start of summer; (3) Ribbonfish: Haijiao, Shenshan, Huadao, Langgang, Erxiongdi, Dinghai, Changtu, from minor snow to major snow; (4) Cuttlefish: Shenshan, Qingbang, Miaozi Lake, Huangxing, Taizhou Islands, from February to June; (5) Reevess shad: Zhoushan Islands, Lvsi Yang, from Pure Brightness to Major Heat; (6) Jellyfish: Sijiao, Huanglong, present in all seasons, more abundant in spring; (7) Horse mackerel: Lvsi Yang, ten days before the Start of Summer to late May. The fishing seasons mentioned above refer to the most prominent species. In reality, fishing continues throughout the year, with only differences in peak and off-peak seasons.

Regular Patrol This office currently has five patrol vessels, which are barely sufficient for fisheries protection. The fisheries protection measures are divided into regular patrol, roving, and escort, which will be carried out simultaneously. Regular patrol will be conducted on a district basis during normal times and on a fishing ground basis during the fishing season. The patrol measures are as follows: (1) One patrol vessel will be assigned to each fishing area for regular patrol; (2) During the peak fishing season, patrol vessels will regularly patrol the fishing grounds; (3) Patrol vessels will be responsible for all security matters within the fishing area and fishing ground and shall not leave unless absolutely necessary; (4) Patrol vessels will only be responsible for protecting fishing operations. The escort of fishing boats will be handled by another patrol vessel; (5) If foreign vessels are found encroaching on fishing grounds, measures should be taken to stop them according to the situation, or the incident should be reported to this office for submission to the Ministry of Industry for review and handling.

Roving and Escort Although each fishing area has a patrol vessel for regular patrol, the fishing areas are vast, and there are concerns that some areas may not be adequately covered. Moreover, the patrol vessels of this office are not equipped with radio stations, which is inconvenient for communication. Therefore, two patrol vessels will be assigned to roving and escort duties. The measures are as follows: (1) The roving area will be temporarily limited to the area from Lvsi Yang in the north to Wenzhou Bay in the south; (2) Roving patrol vessels will be responsible for communication duties for the patrol vessels; (3) If the patrol vessel stationed in a fishing area leaves the fishing area due to necessary circumstances, the roving patrol vessel shall immediately take over the defense of the fishing area; (4) If a large fleet of fishing boats requests an escort due to full loads from fishing or purchasing, the roving patrol vessel shall consider the situation and report to this office for review and handling, or escort them immediately; (5) If foreign vessels are found encroaching on fishing grounds, measures should be taken to stop them according to the situation, or the incident should be reported to this office for submission to the Ministry of Industry for review and handling; (6) Fishing boats are prohibited from fishing in prohibited fishing areas.

Fisheries Survey The patrol vessels patrolling each fishing area are instructed to conduct a detailed survey of the local fisheries and report it to this office for reference. The survey items for each patrol vessel are as follows: (1) Name of the fishing area; (2) Location of the fishing ground; (3) Number of fishing boats; (4) Types of fishing boats; (5) Types of fish products; (6) Estimated value of catches; (7) Fishing time; (8) Sales market; (9) General living conditions of fishermen; (10) General conditions of the fishermen's association (or office); (11) Security conditions of the fishing ground.

Shanghai County Land Consolidation Conference

Discussing the Width of River Courses in Each District

The Shanghai County Land Consolidation Discussion Committee held its seventh meeting yesterday, chaired by Pan Zhongjia. Matters for discussion: (1) Review of the proposed widths of river courses in the Fifth District. Resolution: The county should dispatch eight surveyors to measure the Zhoupu Tang. For the remaining rivers and streams, the heads of each township in the district should be jointly surveyed at the same time as the Zhoupu Tang is measured, and detailed widths should be proposed for review. (2) Should districts that have not proposed widths of river courses be uniformly urged to do so? Resolution: The original resolution to urge each district to submit proposals for review remains in effect. (3) Should the river area of already measured widths be transferred to the land survey team? Resolution: The land survey team should still be instructed to draw a dotted line according to the determined width and separately calculate and report the area of the riverbed and road surface.

The Mingshing to Set Sail on Maiden Voyage on the 9th

Operating on the Three Seas Route

The Lianhe, purchased from Jardine Matheson by the Sanbei Company, has undergone major repairs in the factory since its acquisition. First, second, and third class passenger berths have been added. Construction has taken over three months. The ship's dining room, staterooms, and other facilities have been completely renovated, beautifully decorated, and are even better than the Yongxing. It has been renamed the Mingshing. The ship has a tonnage of 2,770 tons, a registered tonnage of 1,588 tons, a length of 278 feet 2 inches, a width of 42 feet 9 inches, and a horsepower of 1,000. It can travel 10.75 nautical miles per hour. The ship was built by the French CAITLARD & CO. factory in Harfleur. The renovation is now complete, and it can leave the factory on the 8th.

Wharf Completion

Sanbei purchased land in Zhenhai and built a new wharf and warehouse at a cost of 100,000 yuan to operate this new route. Construction began last autumn. The wharf is adjacent to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's Zhenhai wharf. At the time, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company was concerned that the turning of ships would be hindered and negotiated with Sanbei. Later, as there was no hindrance, Sanbei was able to proceed with construction as planned. It is now completed.

Mr. Yu's Inspection

Mr. Yu Qiaqing, general manager of Sanbei, went to Ningbo during the New Year's holiday to inspect the new wharf and warehouse in Zhenhai, a port that is of great importance to the operation of the Mingshing's Three Seas route (Shanghai, Zhenhai, Dinghai). He also met with the managers of Ningbo to discuss plans for the new ship's operation. Mr. Yu has now returned to Shanghai after completing his business.

Inaugural Voyage

After the Mingshing's renovation, the company reported it to the Maritime Administration and the Customs for registration, changed the national flag, ship flag, and crew, which are being assigned. It is expected to be determined in the next day or two and orders will be issued to the ship. The tea boy and middle cabin staff have all been internally appointed. The Mingshing's inaugural voyage will be to Zhenhai and Dinghai, and is scheduled to depart from Shanghai for the first time on the 9th of this month.

Lawyers' Association Jointly Disputes Notification and Delivery Fees

The Shanghai Lawyers' Association received a letter from the Tianjin Lawyers' Association yesterday, stating: "In response to the telegraph from the Wuhan Lawyers' Association, which stated that the Hubei Higher Court issued an order, forwarded from the Ministry of Judicial Administration, regarding the use of summonses and the collection of delivery fees for lawyers appearing in court, this association believes that this is a matter of principle and lacks legal basis, and has filed a petition with the ministry to strongly argue against it. We hope that you will all stand together." Upon receiving this letter, it was immediately submitted to the Standing Councilors' Meeting for discussion. The councilors agreed that, according to Article 44 of the Wuhan Lawyers' Association's charter, approved by the Ministry of Economic Affairs ("The court shall use official letters to notify lawyers to appear in court"), and the supplementary judicial regulations, the charters of the Anhui Huaining, Jiangxi Ganxian, Hunan Shaoyang, and Zhejiang Yongjia Lawyers' Associations also contain the phrase "The court shall use official letters to notify lawyers to appear in court." It is clear that official letters and summonses are two different documents, with different forms and natures. Article 158 of the Civil Procedure Law states that a party's appointment of a litigation agent is based on their professional conduct and is not comparable to a party. Receiving a notice from the court is different from the court directly delivering a document to a party. The collection of fees lacks legal basis and there is no precedent for it. It was unanimously resolved to jointly contact the lawyers' associations of various provinces and request the Lawyers' Association of the Republic of China to negotiate with the ministry to strongly argue against it. We hereby inform you for your reference and hope that you will all stand together to achieve the goal of withdrawing the order to uphold the dignity of the legal profession."

Autopsy Report on a Night Watchman Found Dead from Coal Gas Poisoning

Zhu Guangfa, a 32-year-old man from Anhui, had been working as a night watchman at No. 1210, Lane 245, Mei Bai Ge Road, and resided in a small house at the entrance of the lane. On the night before last, Zhu was suffering from a cold and lit a coal briquette stove next to his bed to keep warm. He tightly closed the doors and windows of the room and went to sleep peacefully. However, due to the lack of ventilation, he died from coal gas poisoning. The following morning, at around 6:00 a.m., Zhao Liansheng, another night watchman at No. 1786, went to visit Zhu and found that he had not yet gotten up. He called out to him, but Zhu did not respond. Zhao became suspicious and pushed open the door, only to find Zhu dead. He reported it to the New Gate Police Station, who sent investigators to investigate. They immediately sent Zhu to Renji Hospital, but were unable to save him. The body was transferred to the Forensic Examination Office on Faelun Road. Yesterday morning, the First Special District Court appointed Prosecutor Tang to the office, who confirmed the body and determined that the deceased, Zhu Guangfa, was a male who died from coal gas poisoning. The body was released to the relative, Xu Quanju, who signed a guarantee.

Verdict on Husband Killing Adulterer Case

Liu Bao Given One Year and Nine Months Imprisonment

Liu Bao You, a native of Siyang, Xuzhou, is a clerk residing at No. 29, Maggie Road, Maggie Lane, French Concession, third floor, front building. He is twenty-nine years old this year. His wife, Yang Xiaomei, twenty-two years old this year, had an affair with He Shifa, a native of Nanjing who resides at No. 176 Jules Pasteau Road and works as a chief clerk. At 8:30 p.m. on December 19th of last year, Liu returned home from work and caught He in the room. The two began to quarrel, and He insulted and cursed Liu. In a fit of anger, Liu struck He in the temple with a small iron hammer, causing a fatal injury before medical treatment could be administered. After the incident, the French police sent detectives to arrest Liu. He's widow, He Gengshi, accused Liu of murdering for money. The police sent Liu to the Special Court No. 2, where the lawyer representing the police department charged him with the crime of causing death by injury. He Gengshi also filed an incidental private lawsuit, seeking damages of over 10,000 yuan. After Judge Zhang Chaozuo held several court sessions, gathering witnesses and evidence for investigation, and appointed lawyer Yang Shaopeng to defend the defendant, he announced the conclusion and instructed the parties to wait for a scheduled sentencing. This was previously reported. Yesterday, the date for sentencing arrived. Judge Zhang presided over the criminal division, ordered the defendant Liu Bao You to be brought to court, briefly questioned him, and then sentenced Liu Bao You to one year and nine months of imprisonment for causing death by injury. The number of days of pre-trial detention shall be counted, with two days equaling one day of imprisonment. The incidental civil lawsuit was transferred to the civil division of this court for trial. After the sentencing, the defendant was transferred to the detention center to await instructions during the appeal period.

Large Amount of Morphine Seized from Passengers on Datong Steamer

Fake West Lake Lotus Root Powder

Yi Qiusheng Bribery Case Transferred to Bureau

Chen Zhirong and other police officers of the Municipal Public Security Bureau's Water Patrol Team, at around 12 o'clock the night before last, saw the Datong steamer docked at the Wangjia Wharf. Not yet set to sail, they boarded the ship to inspect the passengers. They noticed two large paper packages and a hand-carried leather suitcase placed near a berth in the third-class cabin, which appeared suspicious. They used an iron rod to pierce into the packages for testing and detected the smell of narcotics. After opening the two paper packages one by one, they found that the top layer contained soft candies, chewing gum, and other sweets. Upon closer inspection, they discovered six large packages of narcotic powder attached underneath, weighing about ninety taels. There were also seven paper boxes of West Lake Lotus Root Powder produced by Taikang Company, but inside were seven large packages of morphine, weighing about eighty taels, worth several thousand yuan. The two ends of the packages were stamped with the fire lacquer seal of Yun Sen Shen Zhuang. Upon opening another leather suitcase, two flannel shirts and a pair of galoshes were found inside. They asked the tea server on the ship about the owner of the items. According to the tea server, the berth was reserved by a Zhenjiang customer, and the paper packages and leather suitcase were also brought by the customer, but the customer had gone ashore for some business. The police officers rewrapped the seized drugs, put them back in their original place, and waited for a long time until the customer arrived. They immediately arrested him. Unexpectedly, the customer suddenly took out twenty-two silver dollars to bribe them, begging to be spared arrest. The police officers brought the bribe money along with the seized evidence back to the team. During the preliminary hearing by Chief Zhu, the suspect identified himself as Yi Qiusheng, 32 years old, a native of Zhenjiang. He had previously opened a cigarette and paper shop outside the South Gate of Tongzhou. He claimed that the drugs did not belong to him and that he had offered the bribe in desperation during the police inspection. Considering the case involved smuggling a large quantity of drugs, it was ordered to prepare a document and submit it to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for strict investigation and punishment yesterday morning.

Until the end of July this year

The police immediately sent detectives to arrest him, but the man had already fled. They prepared a document along with one confession, two threatening letters, two baskets of charcoal, two halves of a receipt, one carrying pole, and two ropes, and transferred them to the bureau for investigation.

The disaster situation is particularly severe in eastern Zhejiang. The land is barren for thousands of miles, and there is almost no harvest. People are crying for food and shivering from the cold. The tragic scene is unprecedented. Mencius said, 'Compassion is in everyone's heart.' Can we not be generous to these disaster-stricken people who are crying for food? Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces have always been known for their rich products, and the prosperity of various industries in Shanghai is also linked to this. Now that Zhejiang Province has suffered this unprecedented catastrophe, we cannot turn a blind eye and fail to seek ways to provide relief. The organizers of the Jiaxu All-Zhejiang Disaster Relief Association have been deeply disturbed by the tragedy. In addition to making every effort to solicit donations from all walks of life, we also aim to gather every bit of help. We have specially joined hands with the Chinese National Products Manufacturers' Association to initiate the Shanghai National Goods Movement Commission-Based Charity Conference. A certain percentage of the participating manufacturers' business income will be donated to the disaster relief fund, which will serve to expand the promotion of national goods and seek to provide relief to the disaster-stricken people from the depths of water and fire. The method is good and the intention is kind, and it is truly a win-win situation. The vacant lot at the intersection of Edinburgh Road and Min Ti Ni Yin Road has been designated as the venue, and the opening ceremony is scheduled for January 15th. Registration will begin immediately. We have always known that your factory's products are excellent and surpass imported goods, and you have spared no effort in the national goods movement. We hope that you will also be happy to agree to participate in this National Goods Movement Commission-Based Charity Conference to jointly support this good cause.

Dr. Su Jielang, founder of the Family Industrial Society and the Children's Dental Clinic, was a native of Gulangyu, Xiamen. After returning from Japan, he devoted himself to the development of dentistry in China. The Children's Dental Clinic is the result of Dr. Su's efforts. Who can compare to Dr. Su in sacrificing personal interests to complete social undertakings? Such a talented person unfortunately passed away on the 23rd of last month due to typhoid fever. Robbery at the Star Weaving Factory

At around 10 AM yesterday morning, four robbers armed with pistols suddenly appeared at the Star Weaving Factory in Dexing South Lane, Nanxiangfen Lane, in the Public Concession, and committed a robbery. One robber stood guard at the entrance, while the other three rushed into the factory's warehouse. Finding nothing to steal, they turned to the accounting room, held the employees at gunpoint, and forced them to hand over the key to the silver box. They stole approximately two hundred and several tens of yuan in cash from the silver box, and then fled. By the time the factory employees chased after them, they had already vanished. The factory owner reported the incident to the relevant police station, requesting an investigation and apprehension.

Three Indians Sue Li Bin for Fraud

Collecting Security Deposits and Hiring Gatekeepers

Then Switching to IOUs and Ignoring the Matter

Li Bin, a 49-year-old Tianjin native and traditional Chinese medicine practitioner residing at No. 9, Lane 40, Danshui Road, has recently been sued in the Criminal Division of the French Police by three Indians, A. Arsen, A. Accasen, and S. Wensen, residing at No. 167, Park Road, in the Public Concession, for fraudulently obtaining money. Li Bin's younger brother, Li Pengcheng, opened the Fu Hui Silver Shop at No. 107-109, Route Cardinal Mercier, in the French Concession, and hired Indian gatekeepers. On October 15th of last year, Li Bin told the Indians that he was going to open the Da Mei Printing Bureau at No. 113, Avenue Joffre, and needed to hire three Indian gatekeepers, and asked them to recommend candidates. The Indians recommended the three plaintiffs. At that time, Li Bin collected security deposits of 1,400 yuan from A. Arsen, A. Accasen, and S. Wensen. The three Indians complied and paid the full amount. Li Bin issued a receipt and ordered A. Arsen to start work first.

The Siming Bank's Inspection Report on Issuance Reserves as of December 31, Year 23 states: "This bank's banknote issuance is fully reserved, with a minimum of 60% in cash reserves and a maximum of 40% in guarantee reserves." The report, after inspection by accountants Wu Zheng and Pan Zhaobang, and supervisors Xiang Fenghou and Xu Boxiong, is as follows: Total amount of exchange coupons issued: 18,310,300 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 18,310,300 yuan. This includes: Amount issued by this bank: 11,810,300 yuan. Reserves: 9,240,300 yuan in cash and 2,570,000 yuan in guarantees. Amount used by fellow banks: 6,500,000 yuan. Reserves: 4,340,000 yuan in cash and 2,160,000 yuan in guarantees. Accountants: Wu Zheng, Pan Zhaobang. Supervisors: Xiang Fenghou, Xu Boxiong.

The Four Banks Reserve Depository is jointly established by the Yanye, Jincheng, Zhongnan, and Dalu Banks to specifically handle the issuance of Zhongnan Bank banknotes. According to the issuance regulations of the depository, the banknotes are fully reserved, with a minimum of 60% in cash reserves and a maximum of 40% in guarantee reserves. It is announced once a week and audited by the auditors and accountants of the four banks. The 261st announcement of the Shanghai Reserve Depository as of December 29, Year 23 is recorded below: Amount of banknotes in circulation: 31,344,373 yuan. Total amount of reserves: 31,344,373 yuan. This includes: 21,985,573 yuan in cash reserves and 9,358,800 yuan in guarantee reserves.

Pushan Villa Charity Report

In December, Pushan Villa buried a total of 85 large coffins and 2,086 small coffins in both the Northern and Southern Chinese areas of the concessions, and collected 449 sets of bones. This includes: 21 large coffins, 1,159 small coffins, and 56 sets of bones buried at the Zhabei Villa; 495 small coffins and 393 sets of bones collected by the Xieqiao branch and various charitable halls in the Southern City; 56 large coffins and 395 small coffins buried from unclaimed bodies in hospitals and autopsy sites within the concession, as per the instructions of the Public Concession police stations and health department; 2 large coffins received from the Chinese Red Cross Society; 2 large coffins received from Tongren Hospital; 2 large coffins received from Baolong Hospital; 2 large coffins and 37 small coffins received from the Lianyi Charity Association. 999 large and small coffins were distributed. All of the above large and small coffins were transported to the Yizhong cemetery at Datangqiao and other locations for burial, and marked for identification, pending claim. In addition, the White Cross Pushan Maternity Hospital on Xinmin Road, Zhabei, provided medical consultations and medicine to a total of 2,980 patients.

Important Pamphlet from the International Problems Research Association

(Verification of the Manchurian Incident) Published

The International Problems Research Association has recently published a pamphlet entitled (Verification of the Manchurian Incident), written by American Dolfman and published in the American (Harper's) magazine. The Association believes that the report's thorough investigation and precise verification make it an extremely important document on the Northeast Incident. The Lytton Report, while not believing in the incident, did not investigate it deeply, so the truth of the incident has not been officially ascertained. Dolfman's report is the first of its kind since September 18th. Since the Japanese side used the "incident" as a basis for exercising its so-called "legitimate self-defense" rights, the "incident" itself is the fundamental issue of the entire case. The conclusion of this article proves that the "incident" cannot be established, and therefore the Japanese military actions cannot be recognized as self-defense, let alone legitimate. The pamphlet costs 20 cents. Those who wish to read it can purchase it directly from the Association at No. 59, Hong Kong Road.

Human Traffickers Convicted

The five-year-old daughter, Fengying, of Li Lu, a woman from Tongzhou residing at No. 80, Lane 690, East Seward Road, disappeared suddenly at around 4 PM on the previous day. At the time, the other two Indians were promised jobs in about two weeks. A. Accasen and S. Wensen had no choice but to agree. Unexpectedly, on November 1st, A. Accasen and S. Wensen still had not been assigned jobs. When they negotiated with Li, the Da Mei Printing Bureau had already announced its closure. Helpless, Li replaced the security deposit receipts with IOUs. Two months have passed since then, and he has not paid back a single cent. The three Indians discovered that all the valuable items in the Da Mei Printing Bureau had been moved away. When they tried to negotiate with Li, he avoided them. At this point, the three Indians reported Li to the French police for fraudulently obtaining money and requested a formal investigation. The police chief approved the request and sent detectives Jiang Changwen and Yin Baoke to arrest Li Bin and send him to the Second Special District Court for questioning and investigation. The police investigation is now complete. Yesterday morning, Judge Wu Fanglian presided over the trial in the Eighth Criminal Court. The police lawyer prosecuted Li Bin for fraud. The plaintiffs then recounted the details of how they were deceived. The defendant, Li Bin, stated that his friend Shen Ronglu borrowed 700 yuan from the three plaintiffs, and he acted as the guarantor. He denied that the amount was as much as 1,400 yuan and denied committing fraud. After the court questioned both parties in detail, it determined that further investigation was necessary. The case was adjourned to the 9th of this month. The defendant was ordered to provide a 5,000 yuan surety, and was remanded in custody in the absence of a guarantor.

Shi Laosan, a native of Danyang who lived in the same residence, was highly suspected. When questioned, he claimed ignorance, and they argued with each other. At that moment, Chinese detective Zhang Youming and detective Huang Fugeng of the Huishan Police Station passed by and inquired about the situation. They took Shi to the police station for interrogation. Shi claimed that Li's daughter had been taken by his friend Zhu Rongkun to the home of Zhang Changsheng, a native of Anhui, at No. 45, Taiping Street, Pudong. The detectives rushed to Pudong, and together with the local police station, they arrested Zhang at the address. Zhang claimed that the girl was at the home of his friend Hua Qianer (a native of Ningbo) at No. 26, Xujiazhai. They then went to retrieve the girl and brought Hua, Zhang, and Shi back to the police station for detention. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special Court. The lawyer for the Public Works Department, Li Zhishan, gave a detailed account of the case's progress. Li Lu testified that her daughter had been abducted. After Judge Xiao Xieffen questioned the defendants and obtained clear confessions, Shi Laosan was sentenced to two years in prison, and Zhang Changsheng and Hua Qianer were each sentenced to six months. Hua's sentence was suspended for two years. Fengying was returned to Li Lu.

Ningbo Delicious Crab Paste Now Available

Crab paste is a specialty of Ningbo, made by fishermen to give as gifts to friends and relatives. It has never been sold on the market. Mr. Xin, the owner of the China Seafood Food Company, is from Donghu, Yin County, and his family has been in the fishing business for generations. He has a unique secret for making it. Now, in order to share it with everyone, he personally takes charge of selecting the fattest crabs and preparing them alive. The taste is light and suitable, with a unique flavor. The paste is transported from the place of origin to Shanghai every day, so it is very fresh. However, it is reported that production is limited and preparation is labor-intensive, so only 500 bottles are available each day. It is sold on consignment at the China National Products Company on Nanjing Road and the Jiufu Nanhua Company on Paoqiu Chang. Those who love this paste are urged to purchase it early to avoid disappointment.

Letter

To the Editor: We are writing on behalf of our client, Ding Peitang, whose family has reported to us that they recently read in the news section of various newspapers on the 5th of this month about the heroin trafficking case cracked in Yunnan Road. The reports state that He Yixiang, Xu Yunlong, and others confessed that Ding Peitang was in charge, which is completely inconsistent with the facts. Upon investigation, He Yixiang, also known as He Yuxiang, borrowed money in 1931 through the introduction of Ding Yunzhou and Ding Ruilin. Despite repeated requests, the debt was not repaid, and a lawsuit was filed with the First Special District Court to recover the debt. Now, because Peitang is currently away dealing with some matters, he has been maliciously framed. We have already telegraphed him to come to Shanghai to file a suit for defamation and clarify the truth. Therefore, we are requesting your newspaper to issue a correction to avoid misleading the public. Sincerely, Lawyer Shen Xuyuan. January 5, 1935.

Nine Games, Nine Wins: Donghua Defeats Shakouer

7-0

In the first round of the Western Union First Division Football League, Donghua created an all-win record with eight wins in eight games. Yesterday, as the second round began, they also defeated Shakouer 7-0 at Yiyuan. Despite the drizzling rain, Donghua continued to score, showing no signs of diminished courage. With nine wins in nine games, there are high hopes for their future in the First Division.

5-0 in the First Half Shakouer kicked off first, but was intercepted by Donghua, who launched a counterattack. After about five minutes, Fu Zhibin cut in from the right. Seeing this, Kamov panicked and tripped him about 30 yards from the goal. Hong Guang took the free kick, sending the ball straight into the goal. The goalkeeper tried to save it, but only touched the edge, unable to stop it. One to zero, Donghua opened the scoring. The young general Fu Zhibin showed his prowess, dribbling in again and shooting into the corner of the goal. Fifteen minutes had passed. Arthur笃 was penalized for a penalty kick. Li Yichen scored a hat-trick, delighting over a thousand fans. Xiao Wan probed from the left, Li Yichen dribbled in and passed the ball secretly. Fu Zhibin scored again. Gu Shangxiang then got another free kick opportunity. The young Fu family player was indeed pleasing, scoring another goal. Five to zero in the first half.

2-0 in the Second Half Center forward Dai was absent due to injury. However, the Donghua tigers were not affected by this, which was also a gratifying matter. After the second half began, Donghua's attacking form seemed to be more moderate, while Shakouer continued to struggle. Seven minutes after the change of ends, Fu Zhibin again hovered in the enemy's rear, seizing the opportunity to pass the ball. Yichen headed the ball in, scoring another goal. In total, Donghua had already scored six goals. Finally, Wan Xianghua passed the ball low to the center, Li Yichen failed to catch it, and Jia Youliang completed the score to 7-0, completing this one-sided match. Shakouer was disheartened.

Donghua:

Shen Yuan Basketball Court Opens; Pirates Defeat National Sports Again

27 to 23, Difference of Four Points

National Sports Team Leaves Shanghai This Morning to Return to Beijing

The newly built Shen Yuan Basketball Court opened at 7:15 PM last night. National Sports and Pirates met for the second time. There were only about 300 spectators. In yesterday's game, both teams were playing away, and the court was large, so the situation seemed very balanced. The Pirates did their best to play their game. In the first half, except for Pirates' Carlson and Smith, who took the lead 2-0 and 4-2 in the first three minutes of the game, the rest of the time National Sports led. However, Li Zhenzhong was guarded by the Pirate leader and could not move freely. The Zhang brothers, working together, took a commanding lead with 6-4 and 8-4. The Pirates panicked and fought hard, resulting in a tie of 11 points each at the end of the first half. In the second half, the Pirates changed their strategy, and the game improved. National Sports did not change its strategy, and the five-man defense failed. Li Zhenzhong's performance declined. The Pirates acted unscrupulously, making many hits with short throws and long shots. Among them, Smith, Shi Xian, and Lain were the most active. As a result, the Pirates won the second victory with a score of 27 to 23.

Amateur Tennis at Death's Door; Pan Lai Denies Rumors

Jakob and Hastings Also Deny New York Reports

(London, 4th, National Telegraph) William O'Brien, an advocate of professional tennis in the United States, claimed that the world's top three male and female tennis stars would join his professional organization. Today, all three players denied the claim. Mrs. Hastings, a member of the British Wightman Cup team, and Mrs. Hatton Jakob, the top American player, both said that O'Brien's remarks were unfounded. Today, the Standard Evening News also received a phone call from Melbourne, Australia, stating that Pan Lai will return to England in April and will maintain his amateur status. According to O'Brien's declaration in New York yesterday, Pan Lai, the world's number one player, has agreed to sign a contract in San Francisco on February 21. Mrs. Hastings has already signed, and Miss Jakob will also sign soon. Pan Lai's compensation is US$40,000, Miss Jakob US$20,000, and Mrs. Hastings US$10,000.

(Melbourne, 4th, Reuters) Today, a Reuters reporter visited Pan Lai, who said that he had never heard of the compensation mentioned in New York and that he did not want to sign any contract until he had returned to London and discussed it with the British Lawn Tennis Association.

(London, 4th, Reuters) Mrs. Hastings stated today that she was unaware of the compensation mentioned by O'Brien and that she did not want to dream of giving up her amateur status. Today, a Reuters reporter visited Tilden to discuss Pan Lai's decision to postpone joining the professional organization until the 1935 Davis Cup is resolved.

(New York, 3rd, National Telegraph) World amateur tennis has suffered another major blow today. According to professional tennis promoter O'Brien, the world's top three male and female tennis stars, Pan Lai, Miss Jakob, and Mrs. Hastings, will all join his professional organization and give up their amateur status. World-renowned stars Tilden, Vines, Richards, Stoeffen, Henton, and others are already in O'Brien's organization. Now, with the addition of these three major stars, their power will be further enhanced. According to O'Brien, Pan Lai will come to San Francisco on February 21 to sign a contract. The compensation will be US$40,000 for Pan Lai, US$20,000 for Miss Jakob, and US$10,000 for Mrs. Hastings. Plans are being made to arrange competitions starting in March of this year. Matches such as Tilden vs. Pan Lai, Pan Lai vs. Vines, and Vines vs. Tilden will surely be the focus of general interest.

Ministry of Education Does Not Allow Extension of Winter Vacation

Reply to Henan and Other Provinces

(Nanjing, 5th, Electric Dispatch) This year's school winter vacation coincides with the end of the lunar year. The education departments of Henan and other provinces, seeing that the winter vacation in North China is longer, have telegraphed the Ministry of Education to cancel the spring vacation and extend the winter vacation. On the 5th, the Ministry of Education replied separately by telegraph that, due to the school vacation regulations, their requests could not be approved.

Ministry of Education Directives on Make-Up Examinations for Students Failing One or Two Subjects

Regarding the petition submitted by the Beiping City Education Association requesting that students who fail one or two subjects in the middle school graduation examination but score above 40 points in each subject be exempted from make-up examinations, the Ministry of Education responded as follows: According to the regulations, students who fail one or two subjects in the middle school examination should retake the failed subjects in the next examination. This has been clearly stipulated by the Ministry and cannot be changed. The number of retakes is limited to two. Students may apply to the educational administrative authority in charge of their original school to request that the educational administrative authority in the area where they are currently studying administer the make-up examination at the time of the examination to avoid students having to travel back and forth. Furthermore, students who have the equivalent academic qualifications of junior high school students may be admitted to schools of a higher grade. If the school to which they are applying admits them according to the quota stipulated by the local educational administrative authority, they will not need to take a make-up examination. Finally, if the university's centralized military training period conflicts with the make-up examination time, other remedies will be found. The request should not be considered, etc. Recently, the Ministry of Education also telegraphed the Sichuan Education Department in response to an inquiry about make-up examinations for students failing one or two subjects, stating that when students who have failed one or two subjects in the middle school examination and have been promoted take make-up examinations for the failed subjects, the education department may request the educational administrative authority in charge of the school to which the students have been promoted to administer the make-up examination on their behalf to avoid difficult travel, etc.

President of Wusong Merchant Marine School Replaced

(Nanjing, 5th, Electric Dispatch) The Ministry of Communications has approved Jian Ting's resignation as president of the Wusong Merchant Marine School, and Wu Daming has been appointed to succeed him.

The newly appointed member of the Sichuan Provincial Government and Director of Education, Yang Quanyu, arrived in Shanghai with his wife a few days ago and visited various universities to inspect their facilities. Having completed his official duties, he and his wife took the early express train to Hangzhou yesterday for an inspection. He is scheduled to stay in Hangzhou for a week before returning to Shanghai to board a ship to take up his new post in Sichuan.

This City's Fourth Senior Middle School Graduation Examination to Commence Tomorrow

Over 700 Students Participating in the Examination and Retake

To Be Held in Four Venues Including Shangwen and Jingye

This city's fourth senior middle school graduation examination is scheduled to be held for three days starting from the 7th of this month. All examination admission tickets have already been announced by the Education Bureau for schools to prepare letters and send personnel to Guizhou Road, Hushou Society to collect them today. The examination times and venues have also been stipulated. Details obtained are recorded as follows:

Examination Times (1) Senior High School Examination Times for Each Subject (Same as Retake Times) January 7th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Foreign Language, 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM History, 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM Biology, January 8th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Mathematics, 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM Geography, 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM Chemistry, January 9th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Chinese Language, 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM Party Principles, 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM Physics, (2) Junior High School Examination Times for Each Subject (Same as Retake Times) January 7th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Foreign Language, 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM History and Geography, 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM Biology, January 8th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Mathematics, 1:00 PM to 2:30 PM Physics and Chemistry, 2:45 PM to 4:15 PM Party Principles, January 9th, 9:00 AM to 12:00 PM Chinese Language,

Venue Allocation: The senior high school graduating class examination venue is at Shangwen Elementary School, the junior high school graduating class examination venue is at Jingye Middle School, the senior high school retake examination venue is at Wanzhu Elementary School, and the junior high school retake examination venue is at Wuben Girls' Middle School. The number of participants is estimated to be 127 in the senior high school section, 191 in the junior high school section, 187 for senior high school retakes, and 201 for junior high school retakes, totaling 706 people.

Important Information for Examinees (1) Examinees must abide by the examination rules within the examination venue. Violators will be given a deduction of points or disqualification from the examination, depending on the severity of the circumstances. (2) For each subject, a bell will ring twenty minutes before the start. Examinees should immediately enter the venue with their admission tickets in order and take their seats according to their examination number. (3) A siren will sound ten minutes before the end of each subject's examination. Examinees who have not finished their papers should immediately finish them as quickly as possible. (4) Examinees exiting the examination venue should rest in the designated rest area and must not wander around arbitrarily, disrupting order. (5) The admission ticket must be carried at all times during the examination period and must not be lost. It should be returned immediately after each subject's examination is completed. (6) After entering the examination venue, the admission ticket must be placed on the table for the proctor to verify. (7) Examinees are responsible for their own meals. Tea and water are provided in each examination venue. (8) Except for necessary stationery, examinees must not bring any other books, papers, or objects into the examination venue. (9) Examination questions and draft paper must not be taken out of the venue. (10) Completed examination papers should be placed on the table and collected by the proctor; no need to submit them personally. (11) After completing the examination paper, examinees must tear off the floating ticket and must not write their name, school name, or any other symbols on the examination paper. Violators will have their examination paper invalidated. (12) All students taking retakes must clearly remember the subjects they are required to retake and enter the venue at the stipulated time and place without confusion.

Examination Rules (1) Examinees must enter the venue with their admission tickets before the stipulated examination time. (2) Late students may be allowed to enter the venue and take the examination within five minutes after the start of the examination; no exceptions will be made after that time. (3) Examinees must bring a writing brush, ink stone, or fountain pen, ink, and mathematics supplies when entering the venue. No other items may be brought in (except for pencils for drawing; no pencils are allowed for anything else). (4) Examinees must take their seats according to their admission ticket number and must not change seats. (5) Each student will only be issued one examination paper for each subject; no replacements will be allowed. (6) During the examination, all instructions from the proctors must be obeyed. (7) During the examination, no questions may be asked, conversations held, or attempts made to look around, leave seats, carry in prohibited items, copy from others, or have someone take the exam in one's place. Violators will not be allowed to participate in the examination. (8) Examinees who need to leave the examination venue temporarily due to special circumstances must obtain permission from the proctor. (9) Examinees must abide by the stipulated examination time and must not extend it. (10) Completed examination papers should be placed on the table and collected by the proctor; examinees must leave the venue immediately.

Female Educator Zhou Huiqing Passes Away

Madam Zhou Huiqing, wife of Zhang Xinbo, principal of Xin Huan Vocational Middle School, was a distinguished student of the Patriotic Women's School. She was particularly well-versed in literature and had many writings, poems, and essays. Fellow villagers regarded her highly. After graduation, she successively served as a teacher at schools such as Haimen Shangping Girls' Middle School and Nantong Third Elementary School. Since marrying Mr. Zhang, the couple has been deeply devoted to each other. Mr. Zhang and his brothers founded Xin Huan Middle and Elementary Schools, and Madam Zhou assisted in the process, successively serving as the director of teaching at Xin Huan Elementary School and the director of affairs at Xin Huan Vocational Middle School, which was particularly laborious. A month ago, when a student contracted scarlet fever, she visited and cared for the student several times, resulting in her being infected and developing diphtheria. She was immediately sent to the Municipal Contagious Disease Hospital for treatment, but to no avail. She passed away in the hospital at 5:00 AM yesterday. It is said that the funeral will be held at 2:00 PM on January 7th at the Shanghai Funeral Home on Xujiahui Road. Our country's female community has lost a talent. It is most regrettable.

Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly

Interest Is the Mother of Success

— Zhu Ming

No matter what a person does, they must have interest. Only then can they do it happily, and only then will what they do develop. Reading is certainly the same.

There are many kinds of school subjects, all of which are common general knowledge of life. It is impossible not to know some of them, so one must have an interest in studying each subject.

However, among all the subjects, each person has their own opinion on which is the most interesting. This varies from person to person, just like eating. Some people like to eat salty foods, while others like to eat sweet foods. Tastes differ, so naturally what they like to eat is also different. This difference is due to the proximity or dissimilarity of individual personalities.

For example, some children like drawing and are particularly interested in it. They have the hope of becoming successful artists in the future. Some children like mathematics and are particularly interested in it. They have the hope of becoming successful mathematicians in the future. If you teach someone who likes drawing to calculate mathematics, they will definitely not calculate very accurately. And if you teach someone who likes mathematics to draw, they will definitely not draw very well. This is because their personalities are not similar, so their interest is not that strong, and their performance is relatively poor.

The personality of the great biologist Darwin was to like studying biology. So in elementary school, although his other subjects were relatively poor, he was not naughty. It was because he felt that his interest in other subjects was not as strong as his interest in biology.

Based on this example, I offer to the children that reading should be of interest. Although some subjects are not suitable for your personality, because they are common knowledge, they should not be ignored. As for subjects that are very suitable for your personality, you should practice them especially, as they are the mother of your future success.

The success of famous people in the world is all due to their childhood interests, coupled with continuous effort. Children, how precious is this interest?

Little Youth League

— Zixi

Ms. Ellen Key clearly told us: The 20th century is the century of the child. That's right, the century of the child. But how to promote the spirit of our children, display the characteristics of our children, and develop the talents of our children?

This semester, eight elementary schools in the Xugongqiao Central Elementary School District have organized a Little Youth League. The purpose of the league is to cultivate character, train the body, and study knowledge. Each league has a leader and a deputy leader. Recently, they have all taken the New Life Movement as a training goal, preparing to become disciplined people under the principles of propriety, righteousness, integrity, and shame.

Recently, a general assembly and a New Life speech contest were held at the central school. The spirit was full, the order was well-maintained, and it was highly praised by local and foreign people.

This winter vacation, they plan to organize a winter defense team with the local people to provide practical services to the public.

Children! Don't be silent anymore! Now is the century of the child. Get up and cheer up!

Good Student

— Cao Meiying, Second Grade Student of Wanzhu Elementary School

Elementary school students, respect teachers, listen carefully to teachers' lectures, and strive to be the first in exams.

Elementary school students, be calm, people respect those who read calmly, and parents are happy in their hearts when they see me.

Elementary school students, be filial, it is most important to respect and love your parents, and remember your parents' teachings in your heart.

Elementary school students, be upright, don't tell lies to deceive people, only then can you be a good student.

Cleaning

— Ling

When I arrived at school the day before yesterday morning, I saw many classmates taking brooms and dustpans to sweep the streets. Everyone was working with great enthusiasm. They had all become temporary street cleaners.

At half past eleven, we began to clean the classroom, sweeping the floor, wiping the glass, wiping the blackboard, arranging the tables, and everyone had a job. For a while, the sound of chaos continued from the classrooms. After twelve o'clock, the classrooms were very different from half an hour ago. Everything was neat and clean, like a bad person suddenly turning into a good person.

Cleaning is to remove dirty things, making this place clean and tidy. It is best to clean people's hearts as well, and not let dirty thoughts remain in the heart.

This cleaning not only made the place clean and made us feel the benefits and methods of cleaning, but also made us feel the fun of this cleaning, and we often helped our mothers sweep at home. In the future, we will develop a habit of diligence, which will be of great benefit to ourselves. If others do not help you sweep, you can do it yourself and not feel difficult. This is truly a gift from the great cleaning.

Mutual Help

— Yi An

Reed Pith Dancing

— Yan Bokuang

Dear children! Have you ever performed at school? Have you ever performed dancing? Dancing is very beneficial for the even development of the muscles and bones of the whole body, and can make the body healthy and beautiful.

But today there is a very fun game, that is, reed pith can also dance. Use a reed pith and pick it into one-inch lengths, and randomly place them on the table. Then use a small square of white paper, smoke it over charcoal fire, put it on the table and immediately rub it with your thumb on the paper several times. While it is hot, move it over the reed pith about half an inch away. The reed pith placed on the table will seem to be dancing, all being sucked onto the paper.

Physics tells us that the paper, heated by the charcoal fire and rubbed by the thumb, generates electricity. The reed pith is attracted by the electric heat.

Improvement of Children's Clothing

— Miaoshen

Whether children are lively or not is partly due to external influences. But it is also different due to different environments. Under the supervision of adults who do not know what children's education is, Chinese children are urged to be (quiet), to sit as upright as adults and listen to speeches. Children have no way to be lively! In addition, the clothes that children wear are all wide robes and long gowns. Since movement is not convenient, there is no way to be lively! This is not because Chinese children are inherently dull, but because adults cultivate their dull appearance. In China, there is no term (children's clothing). Boys wear long robes and mandarin jackets, and sometimes even wear a melon-skin cap. Girls also wear cheongsams that reach the ankles, and their actions have the style of adults. It is naturally difficult to develop a strong body in the future if they have developed sluggish actions since childhood. Let's look at the children in the West. They are all smart and lively. Children have children's clothing. Boys under sixteen or seventeen years old cannot wear trousers; girls under sixteen or seventeen years old cannot wear high heels and women's clothing. Their adults treat children neither casually nor indulgently, but devote most of their energy to children, so that they develop a lively and happy mind and body. This is correct. Children are the future masters of the country!

I think that the clothing of our country's children should be improved as soon as possible. Children should definitely not wear long clothes, and it is also appropriate to wear less. There is a common saying in our country: (If you want your child not to go to the doctor, always keep them slightly cold and hungry.) However, most parents dote on their children and dress them like roly-poly dolls. This actually makes children develop delicate bodies and weak constitutions. Loving them actually harms them. Western children mostly wear at most two or three pieces of clothing, and even wear shorts in winter. Some people say that this is because Westerners are physically strong, so they will not freeze. Chinese people will freeze. Little do they know that if they train their bodies like this from childhood, their bodies can gradually become stronger. As for the style of children's clothing, it is okay to refer to Western styles, or to create new styles. In short, it must be hygienic and meet the needs of children's lively and free movement. Children are our successors, the future masters of the new China. Don't be too indifferent to children!

(2) He tied the sheep to the car, rode on its back, and told the sheep to run faster. (The sheep ran, and the rich man in the car was awakened from his sweet dream, and the laborer in front of the car also fell to the ground.

Apple Clock

— Zhaori

Children, here I am going to teach you a very interesting toy, that is, to make a clock out of an apple. This kind of toy made by your own efforts is much better than selling foreign toys!

Coldest and Hottest

— Yang Bian

Children, what are the coldest things in the world, and where are they? What are the hottest things, and where are they? I think you must often want to know! Okay, now I will report to you.

The coldest place in the world is a small town in northern Siberia called Oymyakon. The temperature there, in the coldest time, is as low as 90.4 degrees below zero Fahrenheit. This cold temperature can freeze mercury.

The temperature in the space between the planets is 454 degrees below zero Fahrenheit, which can be said to be the lowest temperature in nature.

The lowest temperature created by us humans is solid air, and its temperature is 447.8 degrees below zero Fahrenheit, which is not much different from the cold extreme of 459.4 degrees below zero Fahrenheit.

Let's talk about heat. We know that the hottest place in the world is the Sahara Desert, where the temperature reaches a maximum of 736 degrees Fahrenheit. Of course, all living things cannot survive. The center of the Earth is 6,000 degrees Fahrenheit.

The sun is a ball of fire, and its temperature is of course incredibly high. According to Professor Eddington's calculations, the temperature at its center is about 72,000,000 degrees Fahrenheit. Even its outer layer is 3,600 degrees Fahrenheit.

As for the highest temperature created by humans, it is 45,000 degrees, which is a hundred times stronger than sunlight. It is really hot!

Animal Talk

— (Yang Zhen, Fifth Grader of Xunyu Elementary School)

(1) The chicken is very diligent. It always shouts loudly every morning (Brother, get up).

(2) A dog's eyes cannot distinguish colors. When it sees something, it always says repeatedly (Yellow, yellow, yellow).

(3) The sheep is very filial, often shouting (Mama, Mama).

(4) The duck is an optimist, and you can often hear its laughing sound (Hahahaha).

(5) The cat is greedy. When it sees a mouse, it says happily (Miao, miao).

(6) The frog is a sufferer of a cold. It often (Cock-a-doodle-doo).

(7) The goose has the worst temper. It often scolds people (Stupid, stupid).

(8) The mouse has also gone to college, and is a stutterer. It always says (Know-stop, know-stop).

(9) The pig is big, but it is often so angry that it doesn't even want to speak. It always puckers its mouth (Huhu).

(10) The swallow's speech is also different. When it comes back in the spring, it always says (Good to live, live, live. Not good to live, not live).

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor (1)

— Xin Qing

The Adventures of Sinbad the Sailor is a very famous children's book in Europe. Sinbad sailed seven times, experienced all kinds of hardships, but remained indomitable, overcoming dangers as if they were nothing. This kind of hard-working, adventurous spirit should be introduced to our country's children as an example. Therefore, I have faithfully translated it and contributed it to the Spring and Autumn Children's Weekly.

Sinbad's First Voyage

When my father died, he left me a rich fortune, but after a long time, I squandered my time and money in unrestrained indulgence. Finally, I decided to change my life situation, so I sold all my fields and goods and set off with a group of people who were going overseas to trade.

We left Basra on a good ship and set sail for the East Indies. We went everywhere and did very good business with our goods.

One fine and quiet day, we approached a verdant island. According to the leader of the sailors on board, if we wanted to go ashore, we could. We were happy to stretch our legs, so a group of us took a small boat to the shore.

We had a great time on the island because walking on solid ground again was very pleasant. But suddenly, the ground began to shake. The people on the ship saw this and immediately gestured for us to hurry back to the ship. It turned out that what we thought was land was not, but the back of a large whale!

Some of our group had already gotten into the small boat and rowed back to the ship, while others jumped into the sea and swam over; but I was still on the whale's back when it suddenly turned over into the sea.

This put me in a strange situation. I happened to grab a large piece of wood that we had brought for starting fires. If not for this, I would have certainly sunk.

I looked around and saw that my friends had all boarded the ship, and just as a favorable wind rose, the ship immediately set sail; in a short while, it was gone.

This year is the National Children's Year. I hope that all the children of the country will understand their position, strive to be energetic, and work hard to improve themselves. Written by Wu Bixi, age ten.
